# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Key Findings

I've identified **12 critical C++ source files** that define the HTTP filter chain extension mechanism:

### Core Architecture Components:

1. **Filter Interfaces** (`envoy/http/filter.h`):
   - `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` - the mechanism for registering filters
   - `StreamDecoderFilter` and `StreamEncoderFilter` - filter interface contracts

2. **Factory System** (`envoy/http/filter_factory.h`):
   - `FilterFactoryCb` - function type for filter instantiation
   - `FilterChainManager` - the abstraction for applying filter factories
   - `FilterContext` - metadata passed during filter creation

3. **Factory Registry** (`envoy/server/filter_config.h`):
   - `HttpFilterConfigFactoryBase` - base for all HTTP filter factories
   - `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` - downstream filter registration
   - `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory` - upstream filter registration

4. **Filter Chain Management** (`source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h/cc`):
   - `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories` - orchestrates filter chain creation
   - `FilterChainHelper` - processes proto-based filter configurations
   - Manages both static and dynamic (ECDS) filter loading

5. **Filter Execution** (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc`):
   - `FilterManager` - core execution engine
   - `DownstreamFilterManager` - downstream request/response processing
   - `ActiveStreamFilterBase` - per-request filter state and iteration control
   - Maintains ordered filter lists and coordinates sequential execution

   - `NamedHttpFilterFactoryCb` - com

architecture in Envoy v1.31.2 is built on a factory-based registration system with dynamic filter configuration support. The core mechanism consists of several key layers:\\n\\n**1. Filter Interfaces (envoy/http/filter.h)**:\\nDefines the FilterChainFactoryCallbacks interface that allows factories to register filters into the chain. ActiveStreamFilterBase provides per-request filter state and iteration control. FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl implements the FilterChainFactoryCallbacks to handle filter registration within the filter manager.\\n\\n**8. Connection Manager Integration (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc)**:\\nHttpConnectionManagerImpl uses FilterChainFactory to instantiate filter chains for each new HTTP stream.
